## PHASE: P10 dissent-recall builder (#1159) — DIFF gate iter 1 (brief in parallel review). PURE builder only (saturation-loop wiring deferred to I-cred-010b). build_dissent_queries(contradiction_edges, claims, *, max_queries, query_fn): deterministic search-friendly dissent templates ('<subj pred> no effect/contrary evidence/criticism/disputed/limitations') that seek the MINORITY side; deduped, capped at max_queries (env PG_DISSENT_QUERIES_MAX); [] for no edges; optional injected query_fn (LLM seam, mirrors Phase-2) with fail-soft to templates on error. build_source_stratification_plan: ADVISORY per-backend quota hint (never a hard override that could starve consensus); empty for contested_count<=0. ADDITIVE/advisory ONLY — makes NO retrieval call; everything fetched with these queries still passes tier/authority/relevance/strict_verify gates UNCHANGED. default-OFF PG_SWEEP_DISSENT_RECALL; pure, no input mutation. diff --git a/src/polaris_graph/retrieval/dissent_recall_builder.py b/src/polaris_graph/retrieval/dissent_recall_builder.py
```diff
new file mode 100644
index 00000000..5106d72f

+++ b/src/polaris_graph/retrieval/dissent_recall_builder.py
@@ -0,0 +1,133 @@
+"""I-cred-010 (Phase 10, retrieval) — dissent-recall query + stratification builder (pure module).
+
+For a CONTESTED claim (one carrying a Phase-5 ``ContradictionEdge``), BUILD (a) dissent-SEEKING query
+strings that go looking for the MINORITY / contrary side, and (b) an advisory source-type stratification
+plan — so a contested claim ends with real evidence on EACH side, not just the majority view.
+
+POSTURE (binding):
+  * ADDITIVE / ADVISORY ONLY. This module BUILDS queries + a plan; it makes NO retrieval call. Everything
+    a flagged caller eventually fetches with these queries still passes the EXISTING gates — tier
+    classification, ``authority_model.score_source_authority``, ``evidence_selector`` (tier quotas +
+    ``PG_RELEVANCE_FLOOR``), and ``strict_verify`` (the only binding faithfulness gate). Dissent-recall
+    ADDS breadth for the minority side; it NEVER lowers adequacy thresholds, NEVER bypasses authority /
+    relevance scoring, NEVER changes ``strict_verify``.
+  * DEFAULT-OFF byte-identical: ``PG_SWEEP_DISSENT_RECALL`` (no production caller; the saturation-loop
+    wiring is the follow-up I-cred-010b). Empty inputs → empty outputs.
+  * PURE: no network in the builder, no input mutation, deterministic; LAW VI; snake_case. An optional
+    injected ``query_fn`` lets a flagged caller plug an LLM dissent-query generator later (mirrors the
+    Phase-2 injected-judge seam); the default builds NO network call.
+"""
+from __future__ import annotations
+
+import os
+from typing import Any, Callable, Optional
+
+_FLAG = "PG_SWEEP_DISSENT_RECALL"
+_OFF_VALUES = frozenset({"", "0", "false", "off", "no"})
+
+_ENV_MAX_QUERIES = "PG_DISSENT_QUERIES_MAX"
+_ENV_PER_BACKEND = "PG_DISSENT_PER_BACKEND"
+_DEFAULT_MAX_QUERIES = 8
+_DEFAULT_PER_BACKEND = 2
+
+
+def dissent_recall_enabled() -> bool:
+    """True unless ``PG_SWEEP_DISSENT_RECALL`` is unset/falsey (default OFF => byte-identical)."""
+    return os.environ.get(_FLAG, "").strip().lower() not in _OFF_VALUES
+
+
+def _int_env(name: str, default: int) -> int:
+    try:
+        return int(os.environ.get(name, "") or default)
+    except (TypeError, ValueError):
+        return default
+
+
+def _default_dissent_queries(subject: str, predicate: str, text: str) -> list[str]:
+    """Deterministic, search-friendly dissent templates that seek the CONTRARY side of a claim."""
+    base = " ".join(part for part in (subject.strip(), predicate.strip()) if part.strip()).strip()
+    if not base:
+        base = (text or "").strip()[:80]
+    if not base:
+        return []
+    return [
+        f"{base} no effect",
+        f"{base} contrary evidence",
+        f"{base} criticism",
+        f"{base} disputed",
+        f"{base} limitations",
+    ]
+
+
+def build_dissent_queries(
+    contradiction_edges: list,
+    claims: list,
+    *,
+    max_queries: int | None = None,
+    query_fn: Optional[Callable[[str, str, str], list]] = None,
+) -> list[str]:
+    """Pure: emit deduped dissent-seeking query strings for the contested claims, capped at max_queries.
+
+    Returns ``[]`` for no edges (byte-identity when OFF). With an injected ``query_fn`` (subject, predicate,
+    text) -> list[str], a flagged caller can plug an LLM dissent generator; a ``query_fn`` that raises
+    falls back to the deterministic templates for that edge (fail-soft, no crash). NO retrieval call.
+    """
+    if max_queries is None:
+        max_queries = _int_env(_ENV_MAX_QUERIES, _DEFAULT_MAX_QUERIES)
+
+    text_by_sp: dict[tuple, str] = {}
+    for claim in (claims or []):
+        key = (
+            str(getattr(claim, "subject", "") or "").strip().lower(),
+            str(getattr(claim, "predicate", "") or "").strip().lower(),
+        )
+        if key not in text_by_sp:
+            text_by_sp[key] = str(getattr(claim, "text", "") or "").strip()
+
+    out: list[str] = []
+    seen: set[str] = set()
+    for edge in (contradiction_edges or []):
+        subject = str(getattr(edge, "subject", "") or "").strip()
+        predicate = str(getattr(edge, "predicate", "") or "").strip()
+        text = text_by_sp.get((subject.lower(), predicate.lower()), "")
+        if query_fn is not None:
+            try:
+                queries = list(query_fn(subject, predicate, text) or [])
+            except Exception:
+                queries = _default_dissent_queries(subject, predicate, text)
+        else:
+            queries = _default_dissent_queries(subject, predicate, text)
+        for query in queries:
+            normalized = str(query or "").strip()
+            key = normalized.lower()
+            if normalized and key not in seen:
+                seen.add(key)
+                out.append(normalized)
+                if len(out) >= max_queries:
+                    return out
+    return out
+
+
+def build_source_stratification_plan(
+    contested_count: int,
+    available_backends: list,
+    *,
+    per_type_quota: dict | None = None,
+) -> dict:
+    """Pure: an ADVISORY per-source-type quota hint so dissent retrieval is stratified across web /
+    academic / open-access / regulatory — never a hard override that could STARVE the consensus side.
+
+    Empty plan for ``contested_count <= 0`` or no backends (byte-identity). When ``per_type_quota`` is
+    given it is used (filtered to positive quotas on listed backends); otherwise a small even per-backend
+    floor is emitted so each available source type gets some dissent budget.
+    """
+    if contested_count <= 0:
+        return {}
+    backends = [str(b).strip() for b in (available_backends or []) if str(b).strip()]
+    if not backends:
+        return {}
+    if per_type_quota:
+        plan = {b: int(per_type_quota.get(b, 0)) for b in backends}
+        return {b: q for b, q in plan.items() if q > 0}
+    per_backend = max(1, _int_env(_ENV_PER_BACKEND, _DEFAULT_PER_BACKEND))
+    return {b: per_backend for b in backends}

+"""I-cred-010 (Phase 10) — dissent-recall builder. Offline, deterministic, no network."""
+from __future__ import annotations
+
+import pytest
+
+from src.polaris_graph.retrieval.dissent_recall_builder import (
+    build_dissent_queries,
+    build_source_stratification_plan,
+    dissent_recall_enabled,
+)
+
+
+def _edge(subject, predicate):
+    return type("E", (), {"subject": subject, "predicate": predicate,
+                          "claim_cluster_ids": ("a", "b"), "severity": "review"})()
+
+
+def _claim(subject, predicate, text=""):
+    return type("C", (), {"subject": subject, "predicate": predicate, "text": text})()
+
+
+# ── AC-1 ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
+def test_flag_default_off(monkeypatch):
+    monkeypatch.delenv("PG_SWEEP_DISSENT_RECALL", raising=False)
+    assert dissent_recall_enabled() is False
+
+
+@pytest.mark.parametrize("on", ["1", "true", "on", "yes", "TRUE"])
+def test_flag_on(monkeypatch, on):
+    monkeypatch.setenv("PG_SWEEP_DISSENT_RECALL", on)
+    assert dissent_recall_enabled() is True
+
+
+# ── AC-2: no edges -> empty (byte-identity precondition) ─────────────────────
+def test_no_edges_empty():
+    assert build_dissent_queries([], []) == []
+    assert build_source_stratification_plan(0, ["serper", "s2"]) == {}
+
+
+# ── AC-3: queries target the CONTRARY side, deterministic + deduped ──────────
+def test_dissent_queries_target_contrary_side():
+    q = build_dissent_queries([_edge("vaccine", "reduces hospitalization")], [])
+    assert q
+    joined = " ".join(q).lower()
+    assert any(k in joined for k in ("no effect", "contrary", "criticism", "disputed", "limitation"))
+    assert q == build_dissent_queries([_edge("vaccine", "reduces hospitalization")], [])  # deterministic
+    assert len(q) == len(set(q))  # deduped
+
+
+# ── AC-4: max_queries cap + env knob ─────────────────────────────────────────
+def test_max_queries_cap(monkeypatch):
+    edges = [_edge(f"s{i}", "effect") for i in range(10)]
+    assert len(build_dissent_queries(edges, [], max_queries=3)) == 3
+    monkeypatch.setenv("PG_DISSENT_QUERIES_MAX", "2")
+    assert len(build_dissent_queries(edges, [])) == 2
+
+
+# ── AC-5: injected query_fn used; fail-soft to templates on error ────────────
+def test_injected_query_fn_used_and_fail_soft():
+    q = build_dissent_queries([_edge("vax", "x")], [], query_fn=lambda s, p, t: [f"custom {s}"])
+    assert q == ["custom vax"]
+
+    def boom(subject, predicate, text):
+        raise RuntimeError("nope")
+
+    fallback = build_dissent_queries([_edge("vax", "x")], [], query_fn=boom)
+    assert fallback and any("no effect" in x for x in fallback)
+
+
+# ── AC-6: stratification plan ────────────────────────────────────────────────
+def test_stratification_plan():
+    plan = build_source_stratification_plan(2, ["serper", "s2", "openalex"])
+    assert set(plan.keys()) == {"serper", "s2", "openalex"}
+    assert all(v >= 1 for v in plan.values())
+    override = build_source_stratification_plan(2, ["serper", "s2"],
+                                                per_type_quota={"serper": 5, "s2": 0, "x": 9})
+    assert override == {"serper": 5}  # s2=0 dropped; 'x' not a listed backend
+
+
+# ── AC-7 / AC-8: purity — inputs untouched; builder makes NO retrieval call ──
+def test_purity_no_mutation():
+    edges = [_edge("a", "b")]
+    claims = [_claim("a", "b", "text")]
+    build_dissent_queries(edges, claims)
+    assert edges[0].subject == "a" and claims[0].text == "text"
+
+
+def test_builder_imports_no_network_client():
+    """AC-8: the builder BUILDS queries only — it imports no http client, so it cannot fetch/score."""
+    import src.polaris_graph.retrieval.dissent_recall_builder as mod
+    source = mod.__file__
+    text = open(source, encoding="utf-8").read()
+    for forbidden in ("import httpx", "import requests", "openrouter", "run_live_retrieval"):
+        assert forbidden not in text, f"dissent builder must not {forbidden!r} — execution is the caller's"
```

"""I-cred-010 (Phase 10) — dissent-recall builder. Offline, deterministic, no network."""
from __future__ import annotations

import pytest

from src.polaris_graph.retrieval.dissent_recall_builder import (
    build_dissent_queries,
    build_source_stratification_plan,
    dissent_recall_enabled,
)


def _edge(subject, predicate):
    return type("E", (), {"subject": subject, "predicate": predicate,
                          "claim_cluster_ids": ("a", "b"), "severity": "review"})()


def _claim(subject, predicate, text=""):
    return type("C", (), {"subject": subject, "predicate": predicate, "text": text})()


# ── AC-1 ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
def test_flag_default_off(monkeypatch):
    monkeypatch.delenv("PG_SWEEP_DISSENT_RECALL", raising=False)
    assert dissent_recall_enabled() is False


@pytest.mark.parametrize("on", ["1", "true", "on", "yes", "TRUE"])
def test_flag_on(monkeypatch, on):
    monkeypatch.setenv("PG_SWEEP_DISSENT_RECALL", on)
    assert dissent_recall_enabled() is True


# ── AC-2: no edges -> empty (byte-identity precondition) ─────────────────────
def test_no_edges_empty():
    assert build_dissent_queries([], []) == []
    assert build_source_stratification_plan(0, ["serper", "s2"]) == {}


# ── AC-3: queries target the CONTRARY side, deterministic + deduped ──────────
def test_dissent_queries_target_contrary_side():
    q = build_dissent_queries([_edge("vaccine", "reduces hospitalization")], [])
    assert q
    joined = " ".join(q).lower()
    assert any(k in joined for k in ("no effect", "contrary", "criticism", "disputed", "limitation"))
    assert q == build_dissent_queries([_edge("vaccine", "reduces hospitalization")], [])  # deterministic
    assert len(q) == len(set(q))  # deduped


# ── AC-4: max_queries cap + env knob ─────────────────────────────────────────
def test_max_queries_cap(monkeypatch):
    edges = [_edge(f"s{i}", "effect") for i in range(10)]
    assert len(build_dissent_queries(edges, [], max_queries=3)) == 3
    monkeypatch.setenv("PG_DISSENT_QUERIES_MAX", "2")
    assert len(build_dissent_queries(edges, [])) == 2


# ── AC-5: injected query_fn used; fail-soft to templates on error ────────────
def test_injected_query_fn_used_and_fail_soft():
    q = build_dissent_queries([_edge("vax", "x")], [], query_fn=lambda s, p, t: [f"custom {s}"])
    assert q == ["custom vax"]

    def boom(subject, predicate, text):
        raise RuntimeError("nope")

    fallback = build_dissent_queries([_edge("vax", "x")], [], query_fn=boom)
    assert fallback and any("no effect" in x for x in fallback)


# ── AC-6: stratification plan ────────────────────────────────────────────────
def test_stratification_plan():
    plan = build_source_stratification_plan(2, ["serper", "s2", "openalex"])
    assert set(plan.keys()) == {"serper", "s2", "openalex"}
    assert all(v >= 1 for v in plan.values())
    override = build_source_stratification_plan(2, ["serper", "s2"],
                                                per_type_quota={"serper": 5, "s2": 0, "x": 9})
    assert override == {"serper": 5}  # s2=0 dropped; 'x' not a listed backend


# ── AC-7 / AC-8: purity — inputs untouched; builder makes NO retrieval call ──
def test_purity_no_mutation():
    edges = [_edge("a", "b")]
    claims = [_claim("a", "b", "text")]
    build_dissent_queries(edges, claims)
    assert edges[0].subject == "a" and claims[0].text == "text"

"""I-cred-010 (Phase 10, retrieval) — dissent-recall query + stratification builder (pure module).

For a CONTESTED claim (one carrying a Phase-5 ``ContradictionEdge``), BUILD (a) dissent-SEEKING query
strings that go looking for the MINORITY / contrary side, and (b) an advisory source-type stratification
plan — so a contested claim ends with real evidence on EACH side, not just the majority view.

POSTURE (binding):
  * ADDITIVE / ADVISORY ONLY. This module BUILDS queries + a plan; it makes NO retrieval call. Everything
    a flagged caller eventually fetches with these queries still passes the EXISTING gates — tier
    classification, ``authority_model.score_source_authority``, ``evidence_selector`` (tier quotas +
    ``PG_RELEVANCE_FLOOR``), and ``strict_verify`` (the only binding faithfulness gate). Dissent-recall
    ADDS breadth for the minority side; it NEVER lowers adequacy thresholds, NEVER bypasses authority /
    relevance scoring, NEVER changes ``strict_verify``.
  * DEFAULT-OFF byte-identical: ``PG_SWEEP_DISSENT_RECALL`` (no production caller; the saturation-loop
    wiring is the follow-up I-cred-010b). Empty inputs → empty outputs.
  * PURE: no network in the builder, no input mutation, deterministic; LAW VI; snake_case. An optional
    injected ``query_fn`` lets a flagged caller plug an LLM dissent-query generator later (mirrors the
    Phase-2 injected-judge seam); the default builds NO network call.
"""
from __future__ import annotations

import os
from typing import Any, Callable, Optional

_FLAG = "PG_SWEEP_DISSENT_RECALL"
_OFF_VALUES = frozenset({"", "0", "false", "off", "no"})

_ENV_MAX_QUERIES = "PG_DISSENT_QUERIES_MAX"
_ENV_PER_BACKEND = "PG_DISSENT_PER_BACKEND"
_DEFAULT_MAX_QUERIES = 8
_DEFAULT_PER_BACKEND = 2


def dissent_recall_enabled() -> bool:
    """True unless ``PG_SWEEP_DISSENT_RECALL`` is unset/falsey (default OFF => byte-identical)."""
    return os.environ.get(_FLAG, "").strip().lower() not in _OFF_VALUES


def _int_env(name: str, default: int) -> int:
    try:
        return int(os.environ.get(name, "") or default)
    except (TypeError, ValueError):
        return default


def _default_dissent_queries(subject: str, predicate: str, text: str) -> list[str]:
    """Deterministic, search-friendly dissent templates that seek the CONTRARY side of a claim."""
    base = " ".join(part for part in (subject.strip(), predicate.strip()) if part.strip()).strip()
    if not base:
        base = (text or "").strip()[:80]
    if not base:
        return []
    return [
        f"{base} no effect",
        f"{base} contrary evidence",
        f"{base} criticism",
        f"{base} disputed",
        f"{base} limitations",
    ]


def build_dissent_queries(
    contradiction_edges: list,
    claims: list,
    *,
    max_queries: int | None = None,
    query_fn: Optional[Callable[[str, str, str], list]] = None,
) -> list[str]:
    """Pure: emit deduped dissent-seeking query strings for the contested claims, capped at max_queries.

    Returns ``[]`` for no edges (byte-identity when OFF). With an injected ``query_fn`` (subject, predicate,
    text) -> list[str], a flagged caller can plug an LLM dissent generator; a ``query_fn`` that raises
    falls back to the deterministic templates for that edge (fail-soft, no crash). NO retrieval call.
    """
    if max_queries is None:
        max_queries = _int_env(_ENV_MAX_QUERIES, _DEFAULT_MAX_QUERIES)

    text_by_sp: dict[tuple, str] = {}
    for claim in (claims or []):
        key = (
            str(getattr(claim, "subject", "") or "").strip().lower(),
            str(getattr(claim, "predicate", "") or "").strip().lower(),
        )
        if key not in text_by_sp:
            text_by_sp[key] = str(getattr(claim, "text", "") or "").strip()

    out: list[str] = []
    seen: set[str] = set()
    for edge in (contradiction_edges or []):
        subject = str(getattr(edge, "subject", "") or "").strip()
        predicate = str(getattr(edge, "predicate", "") or "").strip()
        text = text_by_sp.get((subject.lower(), predicate.lower()), "")
        if query_fn is not None:
            try:
                queries = list(query_fn(subject, predicate, text) or [])
            except Exception:
                queries = _default_dissent_queries(subject, predicate, text)
        else:
            queries = _default_dissent_queries(subject, predicate, text)
        for query in queries:
            normalized = str(query or "").strip()
            key = normalized.lower()
            if normalized and key not in seen:
                seen.add(key)
                out.append(normalized)
                if len(out) >= max_queries:
                    return out
    return out


def build_source_stratification_plan(
    contested_count: int,
    available_backends: list,
    *,
    per_type_quota: dict | None = None,
) -> dict:
    """Pure: an ADVISORY per-source-type quota hint so dissent retrieval is stratified across web /
    academic / open-access / regulatory — never a hard override that could STARVE the consensus side.

    Empty plan for ``contested_count <= 0`` or no backends (byte-identity). When ``per_type_quota`` is
    given it is used (filtered to positive quotas on listed backends); otherwise a small even per-backend
    floor is emitted so each available source type gets some dissent budget.
    """
    if contested_count <= 0:
        return {}
    backends = [str(b).strip() for b in (available_backends or []) if str(b).strip()]
    if not backends:
        return {}
    if per_type_quota:
        plan = {b: int(per_type_quota.get(b, 0)) for b in backends}
        return {b: q for b, q in plan.items() if q > 0}
    per_backend = max(1, _int_env(_ENV_PER_BACKEND, _DEFAULT_PER_BACKEND))
    return {b: per_backend for b in backends}

+"""I-cred-010 (Phase 10, retrieval) — dissent-recall query + stratification builder (pure module).
+
+For a CONTESTED claim (one carrying a Phase-5 ``ContradictionEdge``), BUILD (a) dissent-SEEKING query
+strings that go looking for the MINORITY / contrary side, and (b) an advisory source-type stratification
+plan — so a contested claim ends with real evidence on EACH side, not just the majority view.
+
+POSTURE (binding):
+  * ADDITIVE / ADVISORY ONLY. This module BUILDS queries + a plan; it makes NO retrieval call. Everything
+    a flagged caller eventually fetches with these queries still passes the EXISTING gates — tier
+    classification, ``authority_model.score_source_authority``, ``evidence_selector`` (tier quotas +
+    ``PG_RELEVANCE_FLOOR``), and ``strict_verify`` (the only binding faithfulness gate). Dissent-recall
+    ADDS breadth for the minority side; it NEVER lowers adequacy thresholds, NEVER bypasses authority /
+    relevance scoring, NEVER changes ``strict_verify``.
+  * DEFAULT-OFF byte-identical: ``PG_SWEEP_DISSENT_RECALL`` (no production caller; the saturation-loop
+    wiring is the follow-up I-cred-010b). Empty inputs → empty outputs.
+  * PURE: no network in the builder, no input mutation, deterministic; LAW VI; snake_case. An optional
+    injected ``query_fn`` lets a flagged caller plug an LLM dissent-query generator later (mirrors the
+    Phase-2 injected-judge seam); the default builds NO network call.
+"""
+from __future__ import annotations
+
+import os
+from typing import Any, Callable, Optional
+
+_FLAG = "PG_SWEEP_DISSENT_RECALL"
+_OFF_VALUES = frozenset({"", "0", "false", "off", "no"})
+
+_ENV_MAX_QUERIES = "PG_DISSENT_QUERIES_MAX"
+_ENV_PER_BACKEND = "PG_DISSENT_PER_BACKEND"
+_DEFAULT_MAX_QUERIES = 8
+_DEFAULT_PER_BACKEND = 2
+
+
+def dissent_recall_enabled() -> bool:
+    """True unless ``PG_SWEEP_DISSENT_RECALL`` is unset/falsey (default OFF => byte-identical)."""
+    return os.environ.get(_FLAG, "").strip().lower() not in _OFF_VALUES
+
+
+def _int_env(name: str, default: int) -> int:
+    try:
+        return int(os.environ.get(name, "") or default)
+    except (TypeError, ValueError):
+        return default
+
+
+def _default_dissent_queries(subject: str, predicate: str, text: str) -> list[str]:
+    """Deterministic, search-friendly dissent templates that seek the CONTRARY side of a claim."""
+    base = " ".join(part for part in (subject.strip(), predicate.strip()) if part.strip()).strip()
+    if not base:
+        base = (text or "").strip()[:80]
+    if not base:
+        return []
+    return [
+        f"{base} no effect",
+        f"{base} contrary evidence",
+        f"{base} criticism",
+        f"{base} disputed",
+        f"{base} limitations",
+    ]
+
+
+def build_dissent_queries(
+    contradiction_edges: list,
+    claims: list,
+    *,
+    max_queries: int | None = None,
+    query_fn: Optional[Callable[[str, str, str], list]] = None,
+) -> list[str]:
+    """Pure: emit deduped dissent-seeking query strings for the contested claims, capped at max_queries.
+
+    Returns ``[]`` for no edges (byte-identity when OFF). With an injected ``query_fn`` (subject, predicate,
+    text) -> list[str], a flagged caller can plug an LLM dissent generator; a ``query_fn`` that raises
+    falls back to the deterministic templates for that edge (fail-soft, no crash). NO retrieval call.
+    """
+    if max_queries is None:
+        max_queries = _int_env(_ENV_MAX_QUERIES, _DEFAULT_MAX_QUERIES)
+
+    text_by_sp: dict[tuple, str] = {}
+    for claim in (claims or []):
+        key = (
+            str(getattr(claim, "subject", "") or "").strip().lower(),
+            str(getattr(claim, "predicate", "") or "").strip().lower(),
+        )
+        if key not in text_by_sp:
+            text_by_sp[key] = str(getattr(claim, "text", "") or "").strip()
+
+    out: list[str] = []
+    seen: set[str] = set()
+    for edge in (contradiction_edges or []):
+        subject = str(getattr(edge, "subject", "") or "").strip()
+        predicate = str(getattr(edge, "predicate", "") or "").strip()
+        text = text_by_sp.get((subject.lower(), predicate.lower()), "")
+        if query_fn is not None:
+            try:
+                queries = list(query_fn(subject, predicate, text) or [])
+            except Exception:
+                queries = _default_dissent_queries(subject, predicate, text)
+        else:
+            queries = _default_dissent_queries(subject, predicate, text)
+        for query in queries:
+            normalized = str(query or "").strip()
+            key = normalized.lower()
+            if normalized and key not in seen:
+                seen.add(key)
+                out.append(normalized)
+                if len(out) >= max_queries:
+                    return out
+    return out
+
+
+def build_source_stratification_plan(
+    contested_count: int,
+    available_backends: list,
+    *,
+    per_type_quota: dict | None = None,
+) -> dict:
+    """Pure: an ADVISORY per-source-type quota hint so dissent retrieval is stratified across web /
+    academic / open-access / regulatory — never a hard override that could STARVE the consensus side.
+
+    Empty plan for ``contested_count <= 0`` or no backends (byte-identity). When ``per_type_quota`` is
+    given it is used (filtered to positive quotas on listed backends); otherwise a small even per-backend
+    floor is emitted so each available source type gets some dissent budget.
+    """
+    if contested_count <= 0:
+        return {}
+    backends = [str(b).strip() for b in (available_backends or []) if str(b).strip()]
+    if not backends:
+        return {}
+    if per_type_quota:
+        plan = {b: int(per_type_quota.get(b, 0)) for b in backends}
+        return {b: q for b, q in plan.items() if q > 0}
+    per_backend = max(1, _int_env(_ENV_PER_BACKEND, _DEFAULT_PER_BACKEND))
+    return {b: per_backend for b in backends}

+"""I-cred-010 (Phase 10) — dissent-recall builder. Offline, deterministic, no network."""
+from __future__ import annotations
+
+import pytest
+
+from src.polaris_graph.retrieval.dissent_recall_builder import (
+    build_dissent_queries,
+    build_source_stratification_plan,
+    dissent_recall_enabled,
+)
+
+
+def _edge(subject, predicate):
+    return type("E", (), {"subject": subject, "predicate": predicate,
+                          "claim_cluster_ids": ("a", "b"), "severity": "review"})()
+
+
+def _claim(subject, predicate, text=""):
+    return type("C", (), {"subject": subject, "predicate": predicate, "text": text})()
+
+
+# ── AC-1 ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
+def test_flag_default_off(monkeypatch):
+    monkeypatch.delenv("PG_SWEEP_DISSENT_RECALL", raising=False)
+    assert dissent_recall_enabled() is False
+
+
+@pytest.mark.parametrize("on", ["1", "true", "on", "yes", "TRUE"])
+def test_flag_on(monkeypatch, on):
+    monkeypatch.setenv("PG_SWEEP_DISSENT_RECALL", on)
+    assert dissent_recall_enabled() is True
+
+
+# ── AC-2: no edges -> empty (byte-identity precondition) ─────────────────────
+def test_no_edges_empty():
+    assert build_dissent_queries([], []) == []
+    assert build_source_stratification_plan(0, ["serper", "s2"]) == {}
+
+
+# ── AC-3: queries target the CONTRARY side, deterministic + deduped ──────────
+def test_dissent_queries_target_contrary_side():
+    q = build_dissent_queries([_edge("vaccine", "reduces hospitalization")], [])
+    assert q
+    joined = " ".join(q).lower()
+    assert any(k in joined for k in ("no effect", "contrary", "criticism", "disputed", "limitation"))
+    assert q == build_dissent_queries([_edge("vaccine", "reduces hospitalization")], [])  # deterministic
+    assert len(q) == len(set(q))  # deduped
+
+
+# ── AC-4: max_queries cap + env knob ─────────────────────────────────────────
+def test_max_queries_cap(monkeypatch):
+    edges = [_edge(f"s{i}", "effect") for i in range(10)]
+    assert len(build_dissent_queries(edges, [], max_queries=3)) == 3
+    monkeypatch.setenv("PG_DISSENT_QUERIES_MAX", "2")
+    assert len(build_dissent_queries(edges, [])) == 2
+
+
+# ── AC-5: injected query_fn used; fail-soft to templates on error ────────────
+def test_injected_query_fn_used_and_fail_soft():
+    q = build_dissent_queries([_edge("vax", "x")], [], query_fn=lambda s, p, t: [f"custom {s}"])
+    assert q == ["custom vax"]
+
+    def boom(subject, predicate, text):
+        raise RuntimeError("nope")
+
+    fallback = build_dissent_queries([_edge("vax", "x")], [], query_fn=boom)
+    assert fallback and any("no effect" in x for x in fallback)
+
+
+# ── AC-6: stratification plan ────────────────────────────────────────────────
+def test_stratification_plan():
+    plan = build_source_stratification_plan(2, ["serper", "s2", "openalex"])
+    assert set(plan.keys()) == {"serper", "s2", "openalex"}
+    assert all(v >= 1 for v in plan.values())
+    override = build_source_stratification_plan(2, ["serper", "s2"],
+                                                per_type_quota={"serper": 5, "s2": 0, "x": 9})
+    assert override == {"serper": 5}  # s2=0 dropped; 'x' not a listed backend
+
+
+# ── AC-7 / AC-8: purity — inputs untouched; builder makes NO retrieval call ──
+def test_purity_no_mutation():
+    edges = [_edge("a", "b")]
+    claims = [_claim("a", "b", "text")]
+    build_dissent_queries(edges, claims)
+    assert edges[0].subject == "a" and claims[0].text == "text"
+
+
+def test_builder_imports_no_network_client():
+    """AC-8: the builder BUILDS queries only — it imports no http client, so it cannot fetch/score."""
+    import src.polaris_graph.retrieval.dissent_recall_builder as mod
+    source = mod.__file__
+    text = open(source, encoding="utf-8").read()
+    for forbidden in ("import httpx", "import requests", "openrouter", "run_live_retrieval"):
+        assert forbidden not in text, f"dissent builder must not {forbidden!r} — execution is the caller's"

.codex/credibility-redesign\p4_diff_gate_verdict_iter2.stderr.txt:946:.\docs\credibility_adaptive_weighting_and_bothsides_recs_2026_06_08.md:1:# POLARIS Source-Credibility & Multi-Perspective Recommendations Report\n### Driving two revisions to `docs/credibility_weighted_sourcing_redesign_plan_2026_06_07.md` — LAYER 1 (scoring) and LAYER 6 (composition + UI)\n\n**Author:** Lead analyst (Claude). **Date:** 2026-06-08.\n**Inputs:** three research streams (per-question adaptive credibility weighting; neutral multi-perspective presentation; friendly UI/artifact patterns).\n**Status:** revision driver. Each layer below states what it **REPLACES** in the Codex-APPROVE'd 2026-06-07 plan, then the concrete mechanism, auditability, reliability, and POLARIS wiring.\n\n**Invariants preserved across both revisions** (these are not negotiable and the revisions do not weaken them): the LLM credibility-judge is **advisory only** — `strict_verify`'s six per-sentence checks (`provenance_generator.py:1156`) remain the binding faithfulness gate; every new layer is **flag-gated, default-OFF byte-identical**, fail-loud on missing inputs; weight is **evidence quality/tier, never headcount**; every displayed aggregate is **one click from the cited `[#ev:id:start-end]` span and its VERIFIED/PARTIAL verdict**; the credibility prior stays **self-computed and verifier-overridable** (no single external rater hardwired); independence-collapse (`synthesis/independence_collapse.py`) still runs before any weighted tally; the contested-topic adjudication **reuses the existing 4-role / voter-arbiter pipeline** (`roles/role_pipeline.py` + `honest_sweep_integration.py`), open-weight voters only — no parallel path is built.\n\n---\n\n## 1. LAYER 1 (scoring): adaptive per-question credibility-skill, replacing the fixed domain-rubric selector\n\n### 1.1 What this REPLACES\n\nThe 2026-06-07 plan's **Phase 2a/2b (L1)** selects one of **three fixed reliability rubrics** (clinical → RCT+peer-review+RoB; econ/policy → design-validity; qualitative → CERQual) keyed off the detected domain. That is still a small lookup table: domain → rubric. The operator constraint is explicit — **replace fixed domain rubrics** with a **generic, domain-agnostic credibility skill the LLM applies by reasoning per question**. Research stream #1's central finding is that the frontier (OpenAI, Gemini, Claude) has already moved this way, and that Perplexity's baked-in EEAT/domain-authority scoring is the closest-to-forbidden counter-example (gameable, popularity-biased, ~60% Google-overlap). We copy the reasoned-generic camp.\n\nThe revision: **domain stops being a selector and becomes context that primes one generic skill.** There is exactly one credibility skill; the detected `scope_template` domain is passed in as a hint the skill reasons over ("this is a clinical efficacy question, so weight trial design and RoB heavily"), not a branch that swaps rubrics. This scales to 10,000+ fields with zero per-field config.\n\n### 1.2 The exact mechanism — credibility-skill / guardrail prompt × (reliability × relevance)\n\n**Step A — deterministic signals (POLARIS produces these; unchanged substrate).** `authority_model.score_source_authority` and `tier_classifier` already emit, per source, the field-agnostic primitives: `authority_score [0,1]`, `source_class`, `corroboration_count` (independent-host agreement), `authority_confidence`, `signal_scores` (the A–E sub-scores), plus `junk_class` / `predatory_oa` (`source_class.py:71-89`). Independence-collapse (`independence_collapse.py`) emits `origin_cluster_id` + canonical-origin designation + copy flag. **None of this is replaced.** These are the inspectable, host-name-free, self-computed inputs (LAW VI: zero host literals in code).\n\n**Step B — the credibility skill consumes those signals and weights them per question.** A new pure prompt module, `authority/credibility_skill.py`, runs a **JudgeRank-style 3-step decomposition** (arXiv 2411.00142) — chosen because each step is inspectable text and is itself the audit template:\n\n1. **Query analysis** — identify what THIS question actually needs (the claim type, what would count as strong evidence for it).\n2. **Source analysis** — for each candidate source, a query-AWARE assessment applying **generic SIFT + lateral-reading + provenance heuristics**, NOT a domain table. The skill's instruction block encodes the domain-agnostic primacy heuristics that are OpenAI's own deep-research pattern: *prefer the primary/official source over an aggregator or SEO blog; prefer the original paper over a survey/secondary summary; corroborate laterally (does independent coverage agree); weigh source incentives/track record; downgrade stale-but-authoritative and retracted/superseded* (the latter wires to the existing `supersession.py` Phase 3 signal).\n3. **Two-axis judgment with rationale** — emit, per source, **RELIABILITY × RELEVANCE** (the EFSA/OHAT weight-of-evidence two-axis, which POLARIS currently conflates into one tier): reliability = internal validity/method given what the skill read in the signals; relevance = directness to this specific question. The product is the per-question credibility weight. **Crucially, the skill is told its priors are the `authority_model` signals and that it may up- or down-weight them with a stated reason** — it does not invent authority from nothing, and it cannot silently override `authority_confidence=LOW` into a fabricated HIGH (thin OpenAlex/ROR signal stays honestly LOW).\n\n**Output schema (machine-parseable, bound to the schema discipline already in §8.3.9):** per source — `{reliability_score, relevance_score, credibility_weight, rationale_string, signals_cited:[...]}`. The weight is **a visible, revisable rationale string, never a hidden scalar and never a fine-tuned-in behavior** (this is why we reject the CAG fine-tune approach from stream #1: opaque learned weights are exactly the auditability failure POLARIS differentiates against — borrow CAG's *evidence* that credibility-conditioning gives noise robustness, and its three generic dimensions of relevance/timeliness/reliability, but implement them at inference time as a prompt-visible signal).\n\n### 1.3 How it stays AUDITABLE (auditable by construction, not bolted on)\n\nThe judgment IS a reasoning trace, so it is emitted verbatim and **bound to the same provenance substrate POLARIS already has**:\n\n- The per-source `credibility_weight` + `rationale_string` + `signals_cited` attach to the source's `AuthorityResult` as **additive fields** (mirroring how `signal_scores`, `junk_class`, `predatory_oa` are already additive side-outputs on the dataclass), emitted on rows in `tier_classifier.py`.\n- At claim time, the weight flows into the four Phase-1/Phase-8 disclosure fields on `SentenceVerification` (`credibility_weight`, `independent_origin_count`, `certainty_label`, `span_verdict`), so each verified sentence shows **which source was weighted how, and why**, one click from its `[#ev]` span.\n- Because the skill cites the deterministic `signals_cited` it reasoned from, the rationale is **checkable against the inputs** — a reviewer can confirm "preferred A over B because A is the primary trial-registry entry and B a secondary news summary" against the actual `source_class` values. The rationale is a **claim to verify, not ground truth** (post-hoc rationalization risk per stream #1) — so it is advisory and the binding gate stays `strict_verify`.\n\nThis is the §-1.1-compliant story: no metadata/count/string-presence signal, every weight traceable to a cited span and an inspectable reason.\n\n### 1.4 Reliability and where it fails (and the guardrail)\n\nStream #1 is blunt about the failure modes, and they bound the design: LLMs "treat all retrieved documents as equally valid" unless explicitly steered and over-rely on high-frequency claims (arXiv 2505.17762); AuthorityBench (2603.25092) shows authority perception is **inconsistent across domains and highly prompt-sensitive**, struggles with false authority, and exhibits position/verbosity/self-preference bias. Therefore:\n\n- **The skill is ADVISORY to ranking/selection, never the faithfulness gate.** It changes *which rows are billed/weighted*, not *whether a sentence verifies its span*. `strict_verify`, 4-role/two-family segregation, and the independent `corpus_approval_gate` tier-distribution backstop all still run sequentially.\n- **Bias mitigations baked into the prompt:** score rationale-first then number; randomize candidate order to blunt position bias; run pointwise (per-source) to avoid listwise permutation instability.\n- **Offline validation before trust:** the chosen judge model+prompt is validated on an **AuthorityBench-style harness** (authority-PERCEPTION only, per the §6a no-overstatement correction — not as a volume-vulnerability benchmark) plus the existing vax adversarial fixture, before it is allowed on the shipping path. Calibration (Brier/ECE) on the emitted weights runs in the existing Phase 11 harness.\n- **Capture resistance:** multi-signal, self-computed, verifier-overridable — no NewsGuard/MBFC/Ad Fontes verdict is hardwired as ground truth (the FTC-capture risk).\n\n### 1.5 The honest gap + exactly what POLARIS builds for L1\n\n**HAVE:** deterministic authority signals (`authority_model`, `tier_classifier`), the additive `AuthorityResult`/`SentenceVerification` schema, independence-collapse, `scope_templates` domain detection, the JSON-verdict schema discipline.\n**MISSING:** the generic per-question credibility skill itself, and the second (relevance) axis.\n**BUILD (revision to Phase 2a/2b):**\n1. `authority/credibility_skill.py` — the pure 3-step (query→source→two-axis-judgment) prompt module emitting `{reliability, relevance, credibility_weight, rationale, signals_cited}`. Domain is an input *hint*, not a rubric switch. (Replaces the fixed-rubric selector in `credibility_prior.py`.)\n2. Add `relevance_score` (and the rationale fields) to `AuthorityResult` (`source_class.py:75`); emit on rows in `tier_classifier.py`.\n3. Wire the skill's weight into the L5 weight-mass tally and the L7 disclosure fields — advisory input, not a gate.\n4. Flag-gated default-OFF byte-identical; OFF = the legacy single-scalar path, byte-for-byte.\n\n---\n\n## 2. LAYER 6 (composition + UI): neutral multi-perspective + transparent evidence-weight artifact, replacing the forewarning/fringe framing\n\n### 2.1 What this REPLACES\n\nThe 2026-06-07 plan's **Phase 7 (L6)** composes contested claims as "consensus at high weight + minority attributed at low weight **with explicit forewarning**, medical-misinfo **low-weight/fringe**, ABSTAIN over fabricated balance." The operator directive is to **replace the forewarning/fringe framing** with a **neutral multi-perspective presentation where competing world-views are shown as legitimate, each carrying its real (possibly asymmetric) evidence weight, and the user judges** — no bias, no stamps, no forewarning prose.\n\n### 2.2 The hard tension, named and resolved (do not skip this)\n\nThere is a real conflict between two binding constraints, and both sides have a lethal failure mode:\n\n- The operator wants **no fringe/forewarning stamp, all sides legitimate, no bias.**\n- The **clinical-safety invariant #5** (binding, preserved) plus Dixon-Clarke 2013 (PubMed 23193194, measured harm: falsely-balanced vaccine reporting *reduced* perceived safety and vaccination intent), Wikipedia FRINGE, and §-1.1 all say **equal treatment of unequal evidence is itself bias** and is "lethal in clinical." I am not authorized to drop invariant #5.\n\n**The reconciliation — handed to us nearly verbatim by all three streams: replace the LABEL with the BASIS.** Wikipedia NPOV's "neutral *editing*, not neutral *content*"; GRADE's "show the basis, let the user infer"; the no-warning rule from stream #2 is satisfiable **if and only if the criteria behind any weight are displayed**. So:\n\n- The **system** stamps nothing — no "fringe," no "debunked," no forewarning sentence. That is the neutrality.\n- The **evidence weight** carries the (often asymmetric) truth, rendered as a visible **per-perspective evidence-basis panel** the user reads and judges. The asymmetry — *14 RCTs + 3 systematic reviews [High]* vs *2 case reports + mechanistic argument [Very Low]* — becomes **visible in the artifact** instead of **asserted in a stamp**. The user infers; the system does not editorialize.\n- "Legitimate" means **shown with its real (possibly low) weight and one-click drill-down to span + verdict** — NOT "shown as equally supported." A genuine world-view dispute with no empirical consensus (values, forecasting) shows steelmanned sides at honest parity; an empirical dispute with consensus shows the real weight distribution.\n- The medical-misinfo case is handled **without the banned word**: its panel is simply **near-empty of independent high-tier basis**, and where there is no independent consensus the claim **ABSTAINs** ("contested; no independent consensus" — reusing existing refuse/unresolved behavior). This preserves invariant #5's *substance* (not normalized as an equal side) while dropping the stamp.\n\nThis is neutral AND anti-false-balance AND §-1.1-safe simultaneously — the operator's "let the user judge" satisfied by *showing the basis*, not by *equalizing the boxes*.\n\n### 2.3 The exact composition mechanism\n\nPer question, the composition path first **diagnoses the contestation type** (this IS the adaptive guardrail, copied from Anthropic's even-handedness "lack-of-consensus" discriminator + OpenAI's seek-the-truth-together):\n\n- **empirical-with-consensus** (vaccines, climate) → due-weight: each side shown, weight proportional to verified-evidence quality; the asymmetry is the message, carried by the basis panel.\n- **genuine-uncertainty** (open scientific questions) → separate *supported* from *open*; sides at honest parity.\n- **values dispute** (politics, ethics) → **steelman each legitimate view** (Ideological Turing Test, neutral terminology, no verdict); no evidence-weight asymmetry asserted because there is no due weight to defer to.\n- **forecasting** (AI-and-jobs) → scenario spread, projective not factual.\n\nEach perspective is gathered through its **own retrieval lens** (MODS-style per-perspective retrieval + citation, arXiv 2502.00322 — raw LLMs silently drop minority views; per-perspective retrieval prevents the drop), then composed via the **existing 4-role / voter-arbiter agreement** (cross-lineage, open-weight voters — the bridging/balanced-panel analog) — **not a new adjudication path**. Reranking-for-balance (arXiv 2506.15925) selects the most balanced faithful candidate, because direct just-prompt-balanced generation empirically skews. **The weight attached to each perspective is evidence QUALITY × independent-origin count, never document count** — else we rebuild Ground News's source-count bias inside the summarizer.\n\n### 2.4 The friendly UI artifact — design\n\nBuilt on the **components that already exist** (#744 citation chip + hover source card, #745 per-claim verdict chip, #747 Proof Replay split-view, #757 report page, #758 claim-anchored compare view) — not designed from scratch.\n\n**The artifact: a claim-anchored "Perspectives" panel** that opens from any contested sentence (reusing the compare-view host), containing per legitimate perspective:\n\n1. **A neutral position header** — "Position held by [who], with this evidence behind it" — no "fringe"/"warning"/"debunked". A steelmanned one-line statement of the view in neutral terms.\n2. **An evidence-basis sub-panel (GRADE-style, the load-bearing element):** the study types / source tiers / independent-origin count behind that perspective, rendered as **frequencies, not a percentage or a lone dot** — "*8 of n: RCTs + systematic reviews [High certainty]*" vs "*2 of n: case reports + mechanistic argument [Very Low]*". The certainty label is acceptable **only because its downgrade criteria are shown** (study design / consistency / directness / independence). This makes the asymmetry self-evident without a stamp.\n3. **Scite-style polarity badges** (supporting / contrasting / contextualizing) on each cited source — **neutral hue + icon + text label, never color alone** (colorblind safety; red=contrasting reads as red=wrong and biases toward consensus — explicitly avoided).\n4. **Drill-down:** every badge, every basis count, every panel is **one click from the raw `[#ev]` span and its VERIFIED/PARTIAL verdict** — the Scite "self-correcting" property: a mis-classified badge is exposed by the citing sentence sitting right behind it, and a meter without drill-down would violate the §-1.1 metadata-audit ban.\n\n**Panel sizing defeats false balance structurally, not with a caveat:** panels are **sized/annotated by real verified-evidence weight**, not equal-width — because equal real estate reads as equal credibility (the false-balance trap), and a caveat is empirically insufficient (Effectiviology / false-balance literature). The asymmetry is *in the layout and the basis panel*, not asserted in prose.\n\n**Three named anti-patterns explicitly rejected** (all from the streams, all as negative templates):\n- **Ground News source-count / coverage bar** — measures who-is-saying-this (volume), not evidence weight; §-1.1 bans source counts as quality signals. If a composition strip is shown at all, its axis is **evidence tier / source type**, never ideology or headcount, and it is kept visually separate from the weight panel so "many sources" never reads as "true."\n- **Bare confidence/credibility score (% or traffic-light dot)** — the best-documented HARM pattern: overconfident displays (80% shown / 70% accurate) pushed AI-advice adoption 57%→69.6%, 64% of users mis-judged calibration, and in a 2025 breast-cancer CDSS high confidence *reduced* diagnostic accuracy via overreliance. POLARIS's honest replacement is the per-sentence VERIFIED/PARTIAL verdict against a real span — never a glanceable dot.\n- **Symmetric 50/50 equal-box presentation** — manufactures false balance; the Dixon-Clarke measured harm.\n\n### 2.5 The honest gap + exactly what POLARIS builds for L6\n\n**HAVE:** the disclosure substrate (per-sentence `[#ev]` tokens, `strict_verify` verdict ladder, `SentenceVerification` additive fields), the existing 4-role/voter-arbiter agreement, independence-collapse for origin-count, and the full UI component kit (citation chip, verdict chip, Proof Replay, compare view).\n**MISSING:** the contestation-type classifier, per-perspective retrieval + composition that defeats false balance by weight, and the Perspectives artifact rendering basis panels.\n**BUILD (revision to Phase 7):**\n1. A **contestation-type classifier** (empirical-consensus / genuine-uncertainty / values / forecasting) priming the composition rule — replaces the fixed forewarning+fringe rule.\n2. **Per-perspective retrieval + balance-rerank composition** over the post-collapse origins, weighting each perspective by verified-evidence quality × independent-origin count (not count).\n3. A **steelman + GRADE-style evidence-basis renderer** feeding a new **claim-anchored "Perspectives" panel** in the compare-view host: neutral headers, frequency-framed basis sub-panels, Scite-style neutral polarity badges, full span-verdict drill-down, weight-proportional sizing.\n4. Validated with a **paired-prompt neutrality eval** (Anthropic's open-sourced political-neutrality harness, adapted so it does NOT reward equal treatment of unequal evidence) + the vax adversarial fixture (asserts the asymmetry renders, no stamp, no 50/50).\n5. Flag-gated default-OFF byte-identical; ABSTAIN reuses existing refuse/unresolved behavior; forewarning prose removed, replaced by the basis panel.\n\n---\n\n## 3. Consolidated "build" summary\n\n| Layer | Replaces (2026-06-07 plan) | POLARIS builds | Binding gate untouched |\n|---|---|---|---|\n| **L1 scoring** | Fixed 3-rubric domain selector (Phase 2a/2b) | `credibility_skill.py` — generic 3-step SIFT/lateral-reading skill, reliability×relevance, rationale bound to `AuthorityResult`/`[#ev]`; domain as hint not switch; `relevance_score` axis | `strict_verify` binding; skill advisory; corpus_approval backstop |\n| **L6 composition+UI** | Forewarning + fringe framing (Phase 7) | Contestation-type classifier + per-perspective retrieval/balance-rerank weighted by quality×origin-count + steelman/GRADE-basis "Perspectives" panel (replace label with basis) | 4-role/voter-arbiter reused (no parallel path); ABSTAIN reuses refuse/unresolved; invariant #5 substance preserved |\n\nHonest residual: L1's skill is prompt-sensitive and must clear offline AuthorityBench-style + calibration validation before it is trusted on the shipping path; L6's steelman is the hardest element to audit mechanically (no test certifies an argument is the strongest version vs a disguised strawman — the paired-prompt eval is the best available check, itself a judgment). Both remain advisory; `strict_verify` carries faithfulness.\n\n---\n\n## 4. .codex/credibility-redesign\p4_diff_gate_verdict_iter2.stderr.txt:1051:.\docs\credibility_adaptive_weighting_and_bothsides_recs_2026_06_08.md:1:# POLARIS Source-Credibility & Multi-Perspective Recommendations Report\n### Driving two revisions to `docs/credibility_weighted_sourcing_redesign_plan_2026_06_07.md` — LAYER 1 (scoring) and LAYER 6 (composition + UI)\n\n**Author:** Lead analyst (Claude). **Date:** 2026-06-08.\n**Inputs:** three research streams (per-question adaptive credibility weighting; neutral multi-perspective presentation; friendly UI/artifact patterns).\n**Status:** revision driver. Each layer below states what it **REPLACES** in the Codex-APPROVE'd 2026-06-07 plan, then the concrete mechanism, auditability, reliability, and POLARIS wiring.\n\n**Invariants preserved across both revisions** (these are not negotiable and the revisions do not weaken them): the LLM credibility-judge is **advisory only** — `strict_verify`'s six per-sentence checks (`provenance_generator.py:1156`) remain the binding faithfulness gate; every new layer is **flag-gated, default-OFF byte-identical**, fail-loud on missing inputs; weight is **evidence quality/tier, never headcount**; every displayed aggregate is **one click from the cited `[#ev:id:start-end]` span and its VERIFIED/PARTIAL verdict**; the credibility prior stays **self-computed and verifier-overridable** (no single external rater hardwired); independence-collapse (`synthesis/independence_collapse.py`) still runs before any weighted tally; the contested-topic adjudication **reuses the existing 4-role / voter-arbiter pipeline** (`roles/role_pipeline.py` + `honest_sweep_integration.py`), open-weight voters only — no parallel path is built.\n\n---\n\n## 1. LAYER 1 (scoring): adaptive per-question credibility-skill, replacing the fixed domain-rubric selector\n\n### 1.1 What this REPLACES\n\nThe 2026-06-07 plan's **Phase 2a/2b (L1)** selects one of **three fixed reliability rubrics** (clinical → RCT+peer-review+RoB; econ/policy → design-validity; qualitative → CERQual) keyed off the detected domain. That is still a small lookup table: domain → rubric. The operator constraint is explicit — **replace fixed domain rubrics** with a **generic, domain-agnostic credibility skill the LLM applies by reasoning per question**. Research stream #1's central finding is that the frontier (OpenAI, Gemini, Claude) has already moved this way, and that Perplexity's baked-in EEAT/domain-authority scoring is the closest-to-forbidden counter-example (gameable, popularity-biased, ~60% Google-overlap). We copy the reasoned-generic camp.\n\nThe revision: **domain stops being a selector and becomes context that primes one generic skill.** There is exactly one credibility skill; the detected `scope_template` domain is passed in as a hint the skill reasons over ("this is a clinical efficacy question, so weight trial design and RoB heavily"), not a branch that swaps rubrics. This scales to 10,000+ fields with zero per-field config.\n\n### 1.2 The exact mechanism — credibility-skill / guardrail prompt × (reliability × relevance)\n\n**Step A — deterministic signals (POLARIS produces these; unchanged substrate).** `authority_model.score_source_authority` and `tier_classifier` already emit, per source, the field-agnostic primitives: `authority_score [0,1]`, `source_class`, `corroboration_count` (independent-host agreement), `authority_confidence`, `signal_scores` (the A–E sub-scores), plus `junk_class` / `predatory_oa` (`source_class.py:71-89`). Independence-collapse (`independence_collapse.py`) emits `origin_cluster_id` + canonical-origin designation + copy flag. **None of this is replaced.** These are the inspectable, host-name-free, self-computed inputs (LAW VI: zero host literals in code).\n\n**Step B — the credibility skill consumes those signals and weights them per question.** A new pure prompt module, `authority/credibility_skill.py`, runs a **JudgeRank-style 3-step decomposition** (arXiv 2411.00142) — chosen because each step is inspectable text and is itself the audit template:\n\n1. **Query analysis** — identify what THIS question actually needs (the claim type, what would count as strong evidence for it).\n2. **Source analysis** — for each candidate source, a query-AWARE assessment applying **generic SIFT + lateral-reading + provenance heuristics**, NOT a domain table. The skill's instruction block encodes the domain-agnostic primacy heuristics that are OpenAI's own deep-research pattern: *prefer the primary/official source over an aggregator or SEO blog; prefer the original paper over a survey/secondary summary; corroborate laterally (does independent coverage agree); weigh source incentives/track record; downgrade stale-but-authoritative and retracted/superseded* (the latter wires to the existing `supersession.py` Phase 3 signal).\n3. **Two-axis judgment with rationale** — emit, per source, **RELIABILITY × RELEVANCE** (the EFSA/OHAT weight-of-evidence two-axis, which POLARIS currently conflates into one tier): reliability = internal validity/method given what the skill read in the signals; relevance = directness to this specific question. The product is the per-question credibility weight. **Crucially, the skill is told its priors are the `authority_model` signals and that it may up- or down-weight them with a stated reason** — it does not invent authority from nothing, and it cannot silently override `authority_confidence=LOW` into a fabricated HIGH (thin OpenAlex/ROR signal stays honestly LOW).\n\n**Output schema (machine-parseable, bound to the schema discipline already in §8.3.9):** per source — `{reliability_score, relevance_score, credibility_weight, rationale_string, signals_cited:[...]}`. The weight is **a visible, revisable rationale string, never a hidden scalar and never a fine-tuned-in behavior** (this is why we reject the CAG fine-tune approach from stream #1: opaque learned weights are exactly the auditability failure POLARIS differentiates against — borrow CAG's *evidence* that credibility-conditioning gives noise robustness, and its three generic dimensions of relevance/timeliness/reliability, but implement them at inference time as a prompt-visible signal).\n\n### 1.3 How it stays AUDITABLE (auditable by construction, not bolted on)\n\nThe judgment IS a reasoning trace, so it is emitted verbatim and **bound to the same provenance substrate POLARIS already has**:\n\n- The per-source `credibility_weight` + `rationale_string` + `signals_cited` attach to the source's `AuthorityResult` as **additive fields** (mirroring how `signal_scores`, `junk_class`, `predatory_oa` are already additive side-outputs on the dataclass), emitted on rows in `tier_classifier.py`.\n- At claim time, the weight flows into the four Phase-1/Phase-8 disclosure fields on `SentenceVerification` (`credibility_weight`, `independent_origin_count`, `certainty_label`, `span_verdict`), so each verified sentence shows **which source was weighted how, and why**, one click from its `[#ev]` span.\n- Because the skill cites the deterministic `signals_cited` it reasoned from, the rationale is **checkable against the inputs** — a reviewer can confirm "preferred A over B because A is the primary trial-registry entry and B a secondary news summary" against the actual `source_class` values. The rationale is a **claim to verify, not ground truth** (post-hoc rationalization risk per stream #1) — so it is advisory and the binding gate stays `strict_verify`.\n\nThis is the §-1.1-compliant story: no metadata/count/string-presence signal, every weight traceable to a cited span and an inspectable reason.\n\n### 1.4 Reliability and where it fails (and the guardrail)\n\nStream #1 is blunt about the failure modes, and they bound the design: LLMs "treat all retrieved documents as equally valid" unless explicitly steered and over-rely on high-frequency claims (arXiv 2505.17762); AuthorityBench (2603.25092) shows authority perception is **inconsistent across domains and highly prompt-sensitive**, struggles with false authority, and exhibits position/verbosity/self-preference bias. Therefore:\n\n- **The skill is ADVISORY to ranking/selection, never the faithfulness gate.** It changes *which rows are billed/weighted*, not *whether a sentence verifies its span*. `strict_verify`, 4-role/two-family segregation, and the independent `corpus_approval_gate` tier-distribution backstop all still run sequentially.\n- **Bias mitigations baked into the prompt:** score rationale-first then number; randomize candidate order to blunt position bias; run pointwise (per-source) to avoid listwise permutation instability.\n- **Offline validation before trust:** the chosen judge model+prompt is validated on an **AuthorityBench-style harness** (authority-PERCEPTION only, per the §6a no-overstatement correction — not as a volume-vulnerability benchmark) plus the existing vax adversarial fixture, before it is allowed on the shipping path. Calibration (Brier/ECE) on the emitted weights runs in the existing Phase 11 harness.\n- **Capture resistance:** multi-signal, self-computed, verifier-overridable — no NewsGuard/MBFC/Ad Fontes verdict is hardwired as ground truth (the FTC-capture risk).\n\n### 1.5 The honest gap + exactly what POLARIS builds for L1\n\n**HAVE:** deterministic authority signals (`authority_model`, `tier_classifier`), the additive `AuthorityResult`/`SentenceVerification` schema, independence-collapse, `scope_templates` domain detection, the JSON-verdict schema discipline.\n**MISSING:** the generic per-question credibility skill itself, and the second (relevance) axis.\n**BUILD (revision to Phase 2a/2b):**\n1. `authority/credibility_skill.py` — the pure 3-step (query→source→two-axis-judgment) prompt module emitting `{reliability, relevance, credibility_weight, rationale, signals_cited}`. Domain is an input *hint*, not a rubric switch. (Replaces the fixed-rubric selector in `credibility_prior.py`.)\n2. Add `relevance_score` (and the rationale fields) to `AuthorityResult` (`source_class.py:75`); emit on rows in `tier_classifier.py`.\n3. Wire the skill's weight into the L5 weight-mass tally and the L7 disclosure fields — advisory input, not a gate.\n4. Flag-gated default-OFF byte-identical; OFF = the legacy single-scalar path, byte-for-byte.\n\n---\n\n## 2. LAYER 6 (composition + UI): neutral multi-perspective + transparent evidence-weight artifact, replacing the forewarning/fringe framing\n\n### 2.1 What this REPLACES\n\nThe 2026-06-07 plan's **Phase 7 (L6)** composes contested claims as "consensus at high weight + minority attributed at low weight **with explicit forewarning**, medical-misinfo **low-weight/fringe**, ABSTAIN over fabricated balance." The operator directive is to **replace the forewarning/fringe framing** with a **neutral multi-perspective presentation where competing world-views are shown as legitimate, each carrying its real (possibly asymmetric) evidence weight, and the user judges** — no bias, no stamps, no forewarning prose.\n\n### 2.2 The hard tension, named and resolved (do not skip this)\n\nThere is a real conflict between two binding constraints, and both sides have a lethal failure mode:\n\n- The operator wants **no fringe/forewarning stamp, all sides legitimate, no bias.**\n- The **clinical-safety invariant #5** (binding, preserved) plus Dixon-Clarke 2013 (PubMed 23193194, measured harm: falsely-balanced vaccine reporting *reduced* perceived safety and vaccination intent), Wikipedia FRINGE, and §-1.1 all say **equal treatment of unequal evidence is itself bias** and is "lethal in clinical." I am not authorized to drop invariant #5.\n\n**The reconciliation — handed to us nearly verbatim by all three streams: replace the LABEL with the BASIS.** Wikipedia NPOV's "neutral *editing*, not neutral *content*"; GRADE's "show the basis, let the user infer"; the no-warning rule from stream #2 is satisfiable **if and only if the criteria behind any weight are displayed**. So:\n\n- The **system** stamps nothing — no "fringe," no "debunked," no forewarning sentence. That is the neutrality.\n- The **evidence weight** carries the (often asymmetric) truth, rendered as a visible **per-perspective evidence-basis panel** the user reads and judges. The asymmetry — *14 RCTs + 3 systematic reviews [High]* vs *2 case reports + mechanistic argument [Very Low]* — becomes **visible in the artifact** instead of **asserted in a stamp**. The user infers; the system does not editorialize.\n- "Legitimate" means **shown with its real (possibly low) weight and one-click drill-down to span + verdict** — NOT "shown as equally supported." A genuine world-view dispute with no empirical consensus (values, forecasting) shows steelmanned sides at honest parity; an empirical dispute with consensus shows the real weight distribution.\n- The medical-misinfo case is handled **without the banned word**: its panel is simply **near-empty of independent high-tier basis**, and where there is no independent consensus the claim **ABSTAINs** ("contested; no independent consensus" — reusing existing refuse/unresolved behavior). This preserves invariant #5's *substance* (not normalized as an equal side) while dropping the stamp.\n\nThis is neutral AND anti-false-balance AND §-1.1-safe simultaneously — the operator's "let the user judge" satisfied by *showing the basis*, not by *equalizing the boxes*.\n\n### 2.3 The exact composition mechanism\n\nPer question, the composition path first **diagnoses the contestation type** (this IS the adaptive guardrail, copied from Anthropic's even-handedness "lack-of-consensus" discriminator + OpenAI's seek-the-truth-together):\n\n- **empirical-with-consensus** (vaccines, climate) → due-weight: each side shown, weight proportional to verified-evidence quality; the asymmetry is the message, carried by the basis panel.\n- **genuine-uncertainty** (open scientific questions) → separate *supported* from *open*; sides at honest parity.\n- **values dispute** (politics, ethics) → **steelman each legitimate view** (Ideological Turing Test, neutral terminology, no verdict); no evidence-weight asymmetry asserted because there is no due weight to defer to.\n- **forecasting** (AI-and-jobs) → scenario spread, projective not factual.\n\nEach perspective is gathered through its **own retrieval lens** (MODS-style per-perspective retrieval + citation, arXiv 2502.00322 — raw LLMs silently drop minority views; per-perspective retrieval prevents the drop), then composed via the **existing 4-role / voter-arbiter agreement** (cross-lineage, open-weight voters — the bridging/balanced-panel analog) — **not a new adjudication path**. Reranking-for-balance (arXiv 2506.15925) selects the most balanced faithful candidate, because direct just-prompt-balanced generation empirically skews. **The weight attached to each perspective is evidence QUALITY × independent-origin count, never document count** — else we rebuild Ground News's source-count bias inside the summarizer.\n\n### 2.4 The friendly UI artifact — design\n\nBuilt on the **components that already exist** (#744 citation chip + hover source card, #745 per-claim verdict chip, #747 Proof Replay split-view, #757 report page, #758 claim-anchored compare view) — not designed from scratch.\n\n**The artifact: a claim-anchored "Perspectives" panel** that opens from any contested sentence (reusing the compare-view host), containing per legitimate perspective:\n\n1. **A neutral position header** — "Position held by [who], with this evidence behind it" — no "fringe"/"warning"/"debunked". A steelmanned one-line statement of the view in neutral terms.\n2. **An evidence-basis sub-panel (GRADE-style, the load-bearing element):** the study types / source tiers / independent-origin count behind that perspective, rendered as **frequencies, not a percentage or a lone dot** — "*8 of n: RCTs + systematic reviews [High certainty]*" vs "*2 of n: case reports + mechanistic argument [Very Low]*". The certainty label is acceptable **only because its downgrade criteria are shown** (study design / consistency / directness / independence). This makes the asymmetry self-evident without a stamp.\n3. **Scite-style polarity badges** (supporting / contrasting / contextualizing) on each cited source — **neutral hue + icon + text label, never color alone** (colorblind safety; red=contrasting reads as red=wrong and biases toward consensus — explicitly avoided).\n4. **Drill-down:** every badge, every basis count, every panel is **one click from the raw `[#ev]` span and its VERIFIED/PARTIAL verdict** — the Scite "self-correcting" property: a mis-classified badge is exposed by the citing sentence sitting right behind it, and a meter without drill-down would violate the §-1.1 metadata-audit ban.\n\n**Panel sizing defeats false balance structurally, not with a caveat:** panels are **sized/annotated by real verified-evidence weight**, not equal-width — because equal real estate reads as equal credibility (the false-balance trap), and a caveat is empirically insufficient (Effectiviology / false-balance literature). The asymmetry is *in the layout and the basis panel*, not asserted in prose.\n\n**Three named anti-patterns explicitly rejected** (all from the streams, all as negative templates):\n- **Ground News source-count / coverage bar** — measures who-is-saying-this (volume), not evidence weight; §-1.1 bans source counts as quality signals. If a composition strip is shown at all, its axis is **evidence tier / source type**, never ideology or headcount, and it is kept visually separate from the weight panel so "many sources" never reads as "true."\n- **Bare confidence/credibility score (% or traffic-light dot)** — the best-documented HARM pattern: overconfident displays (80% shown / 70% accurate) pushed AI-advice adoption 57%→69.6%, 64% of users mis-judged calibration, and in a 2025 breast-cancer CDSS high confidence *reduced* diagnostic accuracy via overreliance. POLARIS's honest replacement is the per-sentence VERIFIED/PARTIAL verdict against a real span — never a glanceable dot.\n- **Symmetric 50/50 equal-box presentation** — manufactures false balance; the Dixon-Clarke measured harm.\n\n### 2.5 The honest gap + exactly what POLARIS builds for L6\n\n**HAVE:** the disclosure substrate (per-sentence `[#ev]` tokens, `strict_verify` verdict ladder, `SentenceVerification` additive fields), the existing 4-role/voter-arbiter agreement, independence-collapse for origin-count, and the full UI component kit (citation chip, verdict chip, Proof Replay, compare view).\n**MISSING:** the contestation-type classifier, per-perspective retrieval + composition that defeats false balance by weight, and the Perspectives artifact rendering basis panels.\n**BUILD (revision to Phase 7):**\n1. A **contestation-type classifier** (empirical-consensus / genuine-uncertainty / values / forecasting) priming the composition rule — replaces the fixed forewarning+fringe rule.\n2. **Per-perspective retrieval + balance-rerank composition** over the post-collapse origins, weighting each perspective by verified-evidence quality × independent-origin count (not count).\n3. A **steelman + GRADE-style evidence-basis renderer** feeding a new **claim-anchored "Perspectives" panel** in the compare-view host: neutral headers, frequency-framed basis sub-panels, Scite-style neutral polarity badges, full span-verdict drill-down, weight-proportional sizing.\n4. Validated with a **paired-prompt neutrality eval** (Anthropic's open-sourced political-neutrality harness, adapted so it does NOT reward equal treatment of unequal evidence) + the vax adversarial fixture (asserts the asymmetry renders, no stamp, no 50/50).\n5. Flag-gated default-OFF byte-identical; ABSTAIN reuses existing refuse/unresolved behavior; forewarning prose removed, replaced by the basis panel.\n\n---\n\n## 3. Consolidated "build" summary\n\n| Layer | Replaces (2026-06-07 plan) | POLARIS builds | Binding gate untouched |\n|---|---|---|---|\n| **L1 scoring** | Fixed 3-rubric domain selector (Phase 2a/2b) | `credibility_skill.py` — generic 3-step SIFT/lateral-reading skill, reliability×relevance, rationale bound to `AuthorityResult`/`[#ev]`; domain as hint not switch; `relevance_score` axis | `strict_verify` binding; skill advisory; corpus_approval backstop |\n| **L6 composition+UI** | Forewarning + fringe framing (Phase 7) | Contestation-type classifier + per-perspective retrieval/balance-rerank weighted by quality×origin-count + steelman/GRADE-basis "Perspectives" panel (replace label with basis) | 4-role/voter-arbiter reused (no parallel path); ABSTAIN reuses refuse/unresolved; invariant #5 substance preserved |\n\nHonest residual: L1's skill is prompt-sensitive and must clear offline AuthorityBench-style + calibration validation before it is trusted on the shipping path; L6's steelman is the hardest element to audit mechanically (no test certifies an argument is the strongest version vs a disguised strawman — the paired-prompt eval is the best available check, itself a judgment). Both remain advisory; `strict_verify` carries faithfulness.\n\n---\n\n## 4.
